This makes hacking a 2FA secured account much harder.\r\n\r\nFor example, when you withdraw money from an ATM machine you present something you have (the credit card) and something you know (the PIN code).","Cold Storage":"Bitcoin wallets that are not connected to the Internet and therefor considered much more secure from theft.","Altcoin":"A General name given to cryptocurrencies other than Bitcoin. For example Litecoin, Ethereum, Dash, etc.","ASIC":"Application Specific Integrated Chip. A chip that was manufactured with the sole purpose of mining Bitcoins.","BIP":"A Bitcoin Improvement Proposal (BIP) is a design document for introducing features or information to Bitcoin. This is the standard way of communicating ideas since Bitcoin has no formal structure.","Bitcoin ATM":"A Bitcoin Automated Teller Machine. Basically this is a machine that accepts fiat money and dispenses Bitcoin in exchange. Some ATMs can also accept Bitcoin and return fiat in exchange. ","Block":"A group of transactions. Each block has a reference to the previous block and that is how a &quot;blockchain&quot; is built.","Blockchain":"The full list of mined blocks since the creation of Bitcoin. There is also a company called Blockchain.info which supplies various Bitcoin services such as a block explorer and a bitcoin wallet but they have no control or authority over Bitcoin's blockchain.","Block explorer":"A block explorer allows you to search and navigate through the blockchain. Using a block explorer you can check the balance of different Bitcoin public addresses, track coin transfer histories watch how many confirmations a transaction has and get a wide variety of statistics about the network such as the current hash rate and more.","ddos attack":"Distributed Denial of Service. An attack orchestrated through the use of multiple computer in order to swamp a network from functioning properly. In Bitcoin for example this can be done by sending massive small amount transactions which will overflow the network and create longer block confirmation times.","Difficulty":"A number which determines how difficult it will be to mine the next block of transactions. Nodes validate the transactions that go throughout the network and they are crucial to keep bitcoin secure and decentralized.","paper wallet":"A type of physical Bitcoin wallet. Inside of keeping the private keys on a piece of hardware, it is written down on a piece of paper. ","private key":"A secret (long) number that allows bitcoins to be spent. The private key is mathematically related to all Bitcoin addresses and public keys generated from it.","proof of stake":"An alternative form to determining mining power. Proof of stake (or POS in short) states that the more you own of a specific cryptocurrency the more mining power you have in its network.","proof of work":"The system used in Bitcoin to decide the amount of mining power each user in the network has. Proof of Work (or POW in short) states that the more computational power you own, the more mining power you will have in the Bitcoin network.","Public key":"A string of long letters and numbers used to create the Bitcoin address. The public key is created from the private key. In cryptography the public key is used to encrypt messages intended only for that key holder.","Scrypt":"An alternative method for mining used in many altcoins. Its main advantage is that it's much more friendly to CPU and GPU mining, making it possible to still mine these coins at home.","SHA256":"The mining method used in Bitcoin's proof of work system.","SPV":"Simplified Payment Verification. A Bitcoin protocol feature that is usually implemented in wallets.       <article id="post-24715" class="post-24715 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail category-services"> 
       <header class="post-header cf"> 
        <div class="heading cf"> 
         <h1 class="post-title item fn" itemprop="name"> Genesis Cloud Mining Review – It’s Not as Profitable as You’d Think </h1> 
         <a href="https://99bitcoins.com/genesis-cloud-mining-review-scam-legit-investment/#comments" class="comments"><i class="fa fa-comments-o"></i> 110</a> 
        </div> 
        <div class="post-meta cf"> 
         <span class="posted-by">By <span class="reviewer" itemprop="author"><a href="https://99bitcoins.com/author/ofirnhm-co-il/" title="Posts by Ofir Beigel" rel="author">Ofir Beigel</a></span> </span> 
         <span class="posted-on"> on <span class="dtreviewed"> <time class="value-title" datetime="2017-04-12T18:35:57+03:00" title="2017-04-12" itemprop="datePublished">April 12, 2017</time> </span> - Updated on <time class="value-title" datetime="April 12th, 2017" title="April 12th, 2017" itemprop="dateModified">April 12th, 2017 </time> </span> 
         <span class="cats"><a href="https://99bitcoins.com/category/reviews-comparisons/services/" rel="category tag">Services</a></span> 
        </div> 
       </header>
       <!-- .post-header --> 
       <div class="post-container cf"> 
        <div class="post-content-right"> 
         <div class="post-content description "> 
          <p>About every other Bitcoin question I get is “should I invest in cloud mining?”</p> 
          <p>I’ve talked a lot about <a href="/?p=23716">Bitcoin investments in the past</a>. One of the things I always tell people who ask me about cloud mining is that I think 99.99% of the companies who offer cloud mining services are probably scams.</p> 
          <p>Meaning, they don’t actually mine Bitcoins with the money you give them, they only use it to pay out other users until the owners run out of money and vanish. However there is 0.01% of companies who actually do run mining hardware and mine Bitcoins for you. Genesis Mining is one of them.</p> 
          <p><a href="/genesis" target="_blank">Genesis mining</a> was founded in 2013 an is one of the oldest Bitcoin companies around. It’s definitely one of the most well known companies when it comes to cloud mining. Genesis has a publicly known mining farm set up in Iceland as shown in this video:</p> 
          <p><iframe src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/nbxay6GjoXc" width="560" height="315" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen></iframe></p> 
          <p>The miners on the farm are able to mine Bitcoin, Ethereum, Dash, Monero, Litecoin and Zcash. However all of the information I brought in this post up until know is somewhat general knowledge. Today I want to dig in deeper into the cloud mining business model and try to answer the question – <strong>is it profitable to cloud mine Bitcoins?</strong></p> 
          <p>Since there are six different currencies that can be mined I want to focus only on Bitcoin cloud mining for the moment since I believe it’s the most popular product on Genesis Mining. Before I begin I just want to mention that <a href="http://www.financemagnates.com/cryptocurrency/bloggers/cloud-mining-put-to-the-test-is-it-worth-your-money/" class="external" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">I did a previous write up</a> on this matter almost 2&nbsp;years ago.</p> 
          <h2><span id="How_does_Genesis_Cloud_Mining_work">How does Genesis Cloud Mining work?</span></h2>
          <div id="toc_container" class="toc_wrap_right no_bullets">
           <p class="toc_title">Table of Contents</p>
           <ul class="toc_list">
            <li><a href="#How_does_Genesis_Cloud_Mining_work">How does Genesis Cloud Mining work?</a>
             <ul>
              <li><a href="#2014-2015_Bitcoin_difficulty_vs_price">2014-2015 Bitcoin difficulty vs. price</a></li>
              <li><a href="#2015-2016Bitcoin_difficulty_vs_price">2015-2016&nbsp;Bitcoin difficulty vs. price</a></li>
              <li><a href="#2016-2017_Bitcoin_difficulty_vs_price">2016-2017 Bitcoin difficulty vs. price</a></li>
             </ul></li>
            <li><a href="#So_should_I_mine_Bitcoins_at_home_instead">So should I mine Bitcoins at home instead?</a></li>
            <li><a href="#What_other_users_are_saying">What other users are saying?</a></li>
            <li><a href="#Genesis_Mining_8211_The_bottom_line">Genesis Mining – The bottom line</a></li>
            <li><a href="#Genesis_Mining">Genesis Mining</a>
             <ul>
              <li><a href="#Profitabliity">Profitabliity</a></li>
              <li><a href="#Transparency">Transparency</a></li>
              <li><a href="#Reputation">Reputation</a></li>
             </ul></li>
           </ul>
          </div> 
          <p>The idea of cloud mining is very simple. Instead of spending thousands of dollars on <a href="/?page_id=16181">Bitcoin mining hardware</a>, you can pay someone to lease their hardware and keep the profits to yourself. The company that&nbsp;rents out the miners takes care of the maintenance and all of the hassle of setting them up.</p> 
          <p>However, you are required to pay a fee for their service but we’ll get to that in a minute. To begin with, I wanted to&nbsp;determine what’s the difference in the ROI (Return Over Investment) between cloud mining and “normal” <a href="/?p=27">Bitcoin mining</a>.</p> 
          <p>At the moment I have 1.19 TH/s with Genesis mining which would cost a new customer around $170 (0.139BTC at today’s exchange rate). This mining capacity generates around 0.00035BTC a day after maintenances are is removed. So at the current BTC price it will take me around 400 days to break even.</p> 
          <p>In the screenshot below you will see different BTC earnings from different contracts. It took me a while and several emails to the company’s support to understand exactly how revenues are calculated and displayed. I would appreciate it though if the fees were mentioned as well so I would be able to see how big they are in relation to the actual payouts.</p> 
          <p><a href="https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/genesis-mining-payouts.png"><img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-24763" src="https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/genesis-mining-payouts.png" alt="genesis mining payouts" width="1077" height="846" srcset="https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/genesis-mining-payouts.png 1077w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/genesis-mining-payouts-300x236.png 300w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/genesis-mining-payouts-768x603.png 768w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/genesis-mining-payouts-1024x804.png 1024w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/genesis-mining-payouts-600x471.png 600w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/genesis-mining-payouts-50x39.png 50w" sizes="(max-width: 1077px) 100vw, 1077px"></a></p> 
          <p style="text-align: center;"><em>each line of BTC payout refers to a different contract. Some of the lines are totals of previous payouts so there are some duplicates listed here. If you’re having a hard time understanding this table (as I had) let me know in the comment section and I’ll do my best to explain.</em></p> 
          <p>The Bitcoin cloud mining contract on Genesis mining is “Open Ended” meaning it will run until it stops being profitable. If you take a look at their customer service page you find the exact definition for it:</p> 
          <blockquote class="modern-quote full">
           <p>In the event of a contract becoming unprofitable (i.e. the payout can’t cover the maintenance fee), the resulting daily payout will be zero. After that, the contract will continue to mine for 60 days. This means that we will take care of the maintenance fee in the hope that your contract becomes profitable again. This may happen if the mining network difficulty decreases and/or Bitcoin price increases. If the contract does not return to profitability in this period it will be terminated because the mining machines are consuming resources (electricity, cooling, hosting, servicing, etc.) which cannot be paid with their generated payouts.</p>
          </blockquote> 
          <p>I.E.&nbsp;the contract will run as long as it can cover maintenance fees which include electricity, cooling, maintenance work and hosting services. And I think this is the thing most people miss.</p> 
          <p>Bitcoin’s difficulty has been more than doubling itself every year for the past 3 years or so. In fact, between 2016 and 2017 it tripled. This means that if you buy a certain package expecting a certain reward, in a year or so you’ll probably be getting anywhere between 33%-50% of that reward. In my case I’ll probably be making 0.00014BTC per day a year from now.</p> 
          <p><a href="https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty.png"><img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-24764" src="https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty.png" alt="Bitcoin difficulty" width="1078" height="771" srcset="https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty.png 1078w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty-300x214.png 300w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty-768x549.png 768w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty-1024x732.png 1024w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty-600x429.png 600w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty-269x192.png 269w, https://99bitcoins.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/Bitcoin-difficulty-50x36.png 50w" sizes="(max-width: 1078px) 100vw, 1078px"></a></p> 
          <p style="text-align: center;"><em>Bitcoin difficulty rate throughout 2014-2017</em></p> 
          <p>So my previous calculation of how much time it will take to recover my initial investment is actually wrong. It would take a lot more than a year, and that’s just to break even.&nbsp;There’s a fair chance&nbsp;my contract will stop becoming profitable before I earn any profits, or that the profits I earn will be very minimal.</p> 
          <p>Of course you could say that there’s the chance that&nbsp;Bitcoin’s price will explode during the next couple of month and then you’ll be profitable way faster. If for example the price goes up to $10,000 I will be able to get my initial $170 in a few months right?</p> 
          <p>Not so sure about that..</p> 
          <p>If price goes up so does difficulty since more people start mining. This means that the Bitcoins you’re making will be worth more but you’ll be making less of them. That’s exactly what happened in 2016 and why the difficulty more than tripled. Here’s the change in price vs difficulty for the past 3 years:</p> 
          <h3><span id="2014-2015_Bitcoin_difficulty_vs_price">2014-2015 Bitcoin difficulty vs. price</span></h3> 
          <p>Bitcoin price: <span style="color: #ff0000;">down 2.45x</span></p> 
          <p>Bitcoin difficulty: <span style="color: #339966;">up 34x</span></p> 
          <h3><span id="2015-2016Bitcoin_difficulty_vs_price">2015-2016&nbsp;Bitcoin difficulty vs. price</span></h3> 
          <p>Bitcoin price: <span style="color: #339966;">up 1.36x</span></p> 
          <p>Bitcoin difficulty: <span style="color: #339966;">up 2.5x</span></p> 
          <h3><span id="2016-2017_Bitcoin_difficulty_vs_price">2016-2017 Bitcoin difficulty vs. price</span></h3> 
          <p>Bitcoin price:&nbsp;<span style="color: #339966;">up 2.29x</span></p> 
          <p>Bitcoin difficulty: <span style="color: #339966;">up 3.05x</span></p> 
          <p>As you can see the difficulty is always going up, no matter what’s happening with the price. And for the past 3 years it’s been going up more than what the price itself has.</p> 
          <h2><span id="So_should_I_mine_Bitcoins_at_home_instead">So should I mine Bitcoins at home instead?</span></h2> 
          <p>If you mine at home with the same hash rate at today’s difficulty you’d be making twice as much (according to our <a href="/?page_id=16186">Bitcoin mining calculator</a>). However, you will be paying for the hardware, cooling and maintenance for yourself. So it’s not safe to say that mining at home would be profitable as well.</p> 
          <p>In the past I’ve written a very detailed post that discusses <a href="/?p=2815">Bitcoin mining profitability</a>. For now let’s just say that if you don’t have any access to cheap electricity and cooling systems I suggest to avoid mining in general and just buy coins instead.</p> 
          <h2><span id="What_other_users_are_saying">What other users are saying?</span></h2> 
          <p>As part of my research for this review I tried to find as many user reviews as possible to get different perspectives. Most, if not all, of the positive reviews I found were accompanied by a promo code. Promo code reviews are questionable in my opinion since the user reviewing gets a commission if you sign up with his promo code, so they have an incentive to write a positive review.</p> 
          <p>One interesting review was from a guy who actually used Genesis Mining to buy Ethereum. He states as follows:</p> 
          <blockquote class="modern-quote full">
           <p>I bought a 1 year contract for 1MH/s ETH mining. I’ve paid 0.11BTC for it (equivalent of 45$ at the time). In one year, Genesis gave me back 2.38ETH (equivalent of 69$ now), so you could say that I’ve made a profit. But you would be wrong!!! That’s just because the price of ETH is high now (29$ versus 12.5$ one year ago).</p> 
           <p>If I would have kept my 0.11BTC, now it would be worth 135$.</p> 
           <p>If I would have bought ETH with the 0.11BTC back then (I would have gotten 3.66ETH, that’s 1.3ETH more than what they gave me back), now it would be worth 106$.</p>
          </blockquote> 
          <p>So even though he could have made a better deal by not investing in Genesis Mining he still made a profit. <em>Please keep in mind that his profit was with Ethereum mining and not Bitcoin mining. In this post I concentrate mostly on Bitcoin mining. Some other altcoins may still be profitable to mine, but I will review them in a different post.</em></p> 
          <p>There are also several <a href="https://bitcointalk.org/index.php?topic=1185909.0" class="external" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">BitcoinTalk posts</a> about the company. It seems that most people claim that you can’t make a profit with their contracts however few supply evidence of actually trying. Bittrust <a href="http://bittrust.org/genesis-mining" class="external" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">shows some positive reviews</a> but I will let you judge for yourselves on their legitimacy.</p> 
          <h2><span id="Genesis_Mining_8211_The_bottom_line">Genesis Mining – The bottom line</span></h2> 
          <p>Finishing up my review about <a href="/genesis" target="_blank">Genesis Mining</a> all I can say is this – The company seems legit but I doubt if it’s a good investment. Seems like I would be much better off just using my money to buy Bitcoins instead of using it for cloud mining contracts. If Bitcoin’s price goes up – I would be making more money, and if it went down, I would be losing less.</p> 
          <p>The one thing that really bothered&nbsp;me though is that Genesis Mining doesn’t seem to share a lot of info regarding my mining performance. I’d except a company that is serious about making money for their investors to supply additional information such as:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>Cloud mining calculators</li> 
           <li>Service fee statements</li> 
           <li>Which blocks were mined and how much was earned on each block (including mining fees)</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>One might suspect that these pieces of information aren’t supplied in order to keep the questionable profitability of cloud mining obscure. If you are invested in Genesis Mining I urge you to contact their support and try to get answers for this (they answer fast from my experience).</p> 
          <p>On a final note, this review is about Genesis Mining but I think you can probably copy and paste its characteristics to most legit cloud mining companies out there. The not so legit mining companies will probably show greater profits because they usually hold stop paying at some point.</p> 
          <p><strong>Keep in mind that this review was made especially for mining Bitcoins, other currencies may still be profitable in these cloud mining schemes.</strong></p>
          <div class="code-block code-block-3" style="margin: 8px 0; clear: both;">

            <div class="review-wu-right"> 
             <div class="pros">
              <h2>Pros</h2> 
              <ul> 
               <li>Fast support</li> 
               <li>Easy to set up</li> 
               <li>Reputable company</li> 
              </ul> 
             </div>
             <!-- end .pros --> 
             <div class="cons">
              <h2>Cons</h2> 
              <ul> 
               <li>Doesn't seem to be profitable in the long run</li> 
               <li>Doesn't supply full information to users</li> 
              </ul> 
             </div> 
            </div>

            <div class="wc-comment-text">
             Here’s the math of Genesis. Lets use a contract mentioned a few times in comments. 100 MH/s. Currently $2799 or $2715 with 3% discount (which one can always get without a code by typing “REVIEW” in order). Currently (July 4th) each MH/s earns 0.000424963 coins. Over the last month coin decay has been roughly 1.5% daily, but I am going to be generous in my calculations and say just 1% decay daily. After 2 years each MH/s will collect 0.042468628 coins, or 100 MH/s will collect 4.246862783 coins. This means that in order to break even after 2 years the

            <div class="wc-comment-text">
             I feel like the problem with the profitability argument is those who are complaining are buying 100 dollar contracts. buy a 13,000 dollar contact getting 100TH/s and see the difference… that’s a current payout of 2400 a month roughly. now the maintenance fee for that H/s is about 28 bucks a day… but that’s still 1600/mo in your pocket.              <div class="wpdiscuz_clear"></div>
            </div>
            <div class="wc-comment-text">
             One rather important point is how much it costs to actually spend the bitcoins you get. Genesis Mining pays out daily to _a lot_ of customers in each transaction. This drives up the transaction fee because your transactions need to refer to _many_ input transactions, and those transactions are huge since they go to so many customers. And who benefits from this? The miners, of course! It is actually in Genesis Mining’s best interest to pay out as often as possible, because their mining will get some of the bitcoins they gave you back. Your money is much better spent
             <span id="wpdiscuz-readmore-54591_0"><span class="wpdiscuz-hellip">…&nbsp;</span><span class="wpdiscuz-readmore" title="Read more »">Read more »</span></span>

               Two fees – depending on what is being mined – upfront and maintenance.                 jQuery(function($) {
                    function equalHeight(group) {
                        tallest = 0;
                        group.each(function() {
                            thisHeight = $(this).height();
                            if(thisHeight > tallest) {
                                tallest = thisHeight;
                            }
                        });
                        group.height(tallest);
                    }

                    equalHeight($(".dg-grid-shortcode .dg_grid-shortcode-col"));

                    $(window).resize(function() {
                        equalHeight($(".dg-grid-shortcode .dg_grid-shortcode-col"));
                    });
                });
            </script>
